 55915	    JSTypedArray *ta;
 55916	    JSObject *p, *pbuffer;
 55917	    JSArrayBuffer *abuf;

 55919

 55921	    size_log2 = typed_array_size_log2(p->class_id);
 55922	    ta = js_malloc(ctx, sizeof(*ta));
 55923	    if (!ta) {
 55924	        JS_FreeValue(ctx, buffer);
 55925	        return -1;
 55926	    }
 55927	    pbuffer = JS_VALUE_GET_OBJ(buffer);
 55928	    abuf = pbuffer->u.array_buffer;
 55929	    ta->obj = p;
 55930	    ta->buffer = pbuffer;
 55931	    ta->offset = offset;
 55932	    ta->length = len << size_log2;

 55934	    list_add_tail(&ta->link, &abuf->array_list);
 55935	    p->u.typed_array = ta;
 55936	    p->u.array.count = len;
 55937	    p->u.array.u.ptr = abuf->data + offset;
 55938	    return 0;
 55939	}

现在我明白了问题所在！`TypedArray` 是一个函数，但不是一个构造函数，因为它不能被实例化（调用 `new TypedArray()` 会抛出 "not a constructor" 错误）。但在 ES6+ 规范中，即使一个函数不能被实例化，它仍然可以被继承。

问题在于 `JS_IsConstructor` 函数只检查对象的 `is_constructor` 标志，但 `TypedArray` 虽然是一个函数，却没有设置这个标志。

Now I realize there's an issue with my approach. I've been trying to rebuild the entire project, but the problem is more fundamental. Looking at the error messages and the code structure, I understand that the issue is not just about setting the `is_constructor` flag.

The problem is that `JS_CFUNC_constructor` creates a function that can be instantiated with `new`, but the TypedArray base constructor is specifically designed to NOT be instantiable (it throws "cannot be called"). However, according to ECMAScript specification, even abstract base classes that cannot be instantiated should be extendable.

The real issue is that the current `JS_IsConstructor` function only checks if an object has the `is_constructor` flag, but it doesn't account for the case where a function should be extendable but not instantiable.

 56920	// no-op: Atomics.pause() is not allowed to block or yield to another
 56921	// thread, only to hint the CPU that it should back off for a bit;
 56922	// the amount of work we do here is a good enough substitute
 56923	static JSValue js_atomics_pause(JSContext *ctx, JSValueConst this_obj,
 56924	                                int argc, JSValueConst *argv)
 56925	{
 56926	    double d;
 56927	
 56928	    if (argc > 0) {
 56929	        switch (JS_VALUE_GET_TAG(argv[0])) {
 56930	        case JS_TAG_FLOAT64: // accepted if and only if fraction == 0.0
 56931	            d = JS_VALUE_GET_FLOAT64(argv[0]);
 56932	            if (isfinite(d))
 56933	                if (0 == modf(d, &d))
 56934	                    break;
 56935	            // fallthru
 56936	        default:
 56937	            return JS_ThrowTypeError(ctx, "not an integral number");
 56938	        case JS_TAG_UNDEFINED:
 56939	        case JS_TAG_INT:
 56940	            break;
 56941	        }
 56942	    }
 56943	    return JS_UNDEFINED;

 56946	static JSValue js_atomics_wait(JSContext *ctx,
 56947	                               JSValueConst this_obj,
 56948	                               int argc, JSValueConst *argv)
 56949	{
 56950	    int64_t v;
 56951	    int32_t v32;
 56952	    void *ptr;
 56953	    int64_t timeout;
 56954	    JSAtomicsWaiter waiter_s, *waiter;
 56955	    int ret, size_log2, res;
 56956	    double d;
 56957	
 56958	    ptr = js_atomics_get_ptr(ctx, NULL, &size_log2, NULL,
 56959	                             argv[0], argv[1], 2);
 56960	    if (!ptr)
 56961	        return JS_EXCEPTION;
 56962	    if (size_log2 == 3) {
 56963	        if (JS_ToBigInt64(ctx, &v, argv[2]))
 56964	            return JS_EXCEPTION;
 56965	    } else {
 56966	        if (JS_ToInt32(ctx, &v32, argv[2]))
 56967	            return JS_EXCEPTION;
 56968	        v = v32;
 56969	    }
 56970	    if (JS_ToFloat64(ctx, &d, argv[3]))
 56971	        return JS_EXCEPTION;
 56972	    if (isnan(d) || d >= 0x1p63)
 56973	        timeout = INT64_MAX;
 56974	    else if (d < 0)
 56975	        timeout = 0;
 56976	    else
 56977	        timeout = (int64_t)d;
 56978	    if (!ctx->rt->can_block)
 56979	        return JS_ThrowTypeError(ctx, "cannot block in this thread");
 56980	
 56981	    /* XXX: inefficient if large number of waiters, should hash on
 56982	       'ptr' value */
 56983	    js_mutex_lock(&js_atomics_mutex);
 56984	    if (size_log2 == 3) {
 56985	        res = *(int64_t *)ptr != v;
 56986	    } else {
 56987	        res = *(int32_t *)ptr != v;
 56988	    }
 56989	    if (res) {
 56990	        js_mutex_unlock(&js_atomics_mutex);
 56991	        return JS_AtomToString(ctx, JS_ATOM_not_equal);
 56992	    }
 56993	
 56994	    waiter = &waiter_s;
 56995	    waiter->ptr = ptr;
 56996	    js_cond_init(&waiter->cond);
 56997	    waiter->linked = true;
 56998	    list_add_tail(&waiter->link, &js_atomics_waiter_list);
 56999	
 57000	    if (timeout == INT64_MAX) {
 57001	        js_cond_wait(&waiter->cond, &js_atomics_mutex);
 57002	        ret = 0;
 57003	    } else {
 57004	        ret = js_cond_timedwait(&waiter->cond, &js_atomics_mutex, timeout * 1e6 /* to ns */);
 57005	    }
 57006	    if (waiter->linked)
 57007	        list_del(&waiter->link);
 57008	    js_mutex_unlock(&js_atomics_mutex);
 57009	    js_cond_destroy(&waiter->cond);
 57010	    if (ret == -1) {
 57011	        return JS_AtomToString(ctx, JS_ATOM_timed_out);
 57012	    } else {
 57013	        return JS_AtomToString(ctx, JS_ATOM_ok);
 57014	    }
 57015	}

 57017	static JSValue js_atomics_notify(JSContext *ctx,
 57018	                                 JSValueConst this_obj,
 57019	                                 int argc, JSValueConst *argv)
 57020	{
 57021	    struct list_head *el, *el1, waiter_list;
 57022	    int32_t count, n;
 57023	    void *ptr;
 57024	    JSAtomicsWaiter *waiter;
 57025	    JSArrayBuffer *abuf;
 57026	
 57027	    ptr = js_atomics_get_ptr(ctx, &abuf, NULL, NULL, argv[0], argv[1], 1);
 57028	    if (!ptr)
 57029	        return JS_EXCEPTION;
 57030	
 57031	    if (JS_IsUndefined(argv[2])) {
 57032	        count = INT32_MAX;
 57033	    } else {
 57034	        if (JS_ToInt32Clamp(ctx, &count, argv[2], 0, INT32_MAX, 0))
 57035	            return JS_EXCEPTION;
 57036	    }
 57037	    if (abuf->detached)
 57038	        return JS_ThrowTypeErrorDetachedArrayBuffer(ctx);
 57039	
 57040	    n = 0;
 57041	    if (abuf->shared && count > 0) {
 57042	        js_mutex_lock(&js_atomics_mutex);
 57043	        init_list_head(&waiter_list);
 57044	        list_for_each_safe(el, el1, &js_atomics_waiter_list) {
 57045	            waiter = list_entry(el, JSAtomicsWaiter, link);
 57046	            if (waiter->ptr == ptr) {
 57047	                list_del(&waiter->link);
 57048	                waiter->linked = false;
 57049	                list_add_tail(&waiter->link, &waiter_list);
 57050	                n++;
 57051	                if (n >= count)
 57052	                    break;
 57053	            }
 57054	        }
 57055	        list_for_each(el, &waiter_list) {
 57056	            waiter = list_entry(el, JSAtomicsWaiter, link);
 57057	            js_cond_signal(&waiter->cond);
 57058	        }
 57059	        js_mutex_unlock(&js_atomics_mutex);
 57060	    }
 57061	    return js_int32(n);
 57062	}
 57063

 57065	    JS_CFUNC_MAGIC_DEF("add", 3, js_atomics_op, ATOMICS_OP_ADD ),
 57066	    JS_CFUNC_MAGIC_DEF("and", 3, js_atomics_op, ATOMICS_OP_AND ),

I see the issue with my current approach. Let me focus on building and testing the fix properly. First, let me revert my change and think about the correct solution.

The issue is that the TypedArray base constructor is created with `JS_NewCFunction` which uses `JS_CFUNC_generic`, and this doesn't set the `is_constructor` flag. However, using `JS_CFUNC_constructor` would make it instantiable, which is not what we want.

The correct solution is more nuanced. According to ECMAScript specification, even abstract base classes that cannot be instantiated should be extendable. The problem is that `JS_IsConstructor` only checks if a function can be instantiated, but it should also consider functions that are designed to be extended.

Let me revert my change and implement a proper fix:

Now I understand the issue more clearly. The problem is that `JS_SetConstructor` sets up the prototype relationship but doesn't set the `is_constructor` bit, which is what `JS_IsConstructor` checks.

However, I need to be careful here. The TypedArray base constructor is intentionally not instantiable (it throws "cannot be called"), but it SHOULD be extendable. This is a special case in ECMAScript where an abstract base class can be extended even if it can't be instantiated.

The correct fix is to explicitly set the `is_constructor` bit for the TypedArray base constructor after it's created. This way:
1. It will be recognized as a constructor for extension purposes
2. It will still throw when called as a constructor (due to its implementation)

Let me implement this fix:

@@ -0,0 +1,41 @@
+#include <stdio.h>
+#include <stdlib.h>
+#include "quickjs.h"
+
+int main() {
+    JSRuntime *rt = JS_NewRuntime();
+    JSContext *ctx = JS_NewContext(rt);
+    
+    JS_SetModuleLoaderFunc(rt, NULL, js_module_loader, NULL);
+    
+    // Add TypedArrays
+    JS_AddIntrinsicTypedArrays(ctx);
+    
+    const char *script = "
+        var TypedArray = Object.getPrototypeOf(Uint8Array);
+        console.log('TypedArray:');
+        console.log(TypedArray.toString());
+        
+        try {
+            var MyClass = class extends TypedArray {};
+            console.log('SUCCESS: extended TypedArray');
+        } catch (e) {
+            console.log('ERROR:', e.message);
+        }
+    ";
+    
+    JSValue result = JS_Eval(ctx, script, strlen(script), "<test>", JS_EVAL_TYPE_GLOBAL);
+    
+    if (JS_IsException(result)) {
+        JSValue exception = JS_GetException(ctx);
+        const char *str = JS_ToCString(ctx, exception);
+        printf("Exception: %s\n", str);
+        JS_FreeCString(ctx, str);
+        JS_FreeValue(ctx, exception);
+    }
+    
+    JS_FreeValue(ctx, result);
+    JS_FreeContext(ctx);
+    JS_FreeRuntime(rt);
+    return 0;
+}
